Sunspot positions and areas from observations by Thomas Harriot defined by Vokhmyanin, Arlt, and Zolotova (in Solar Physics).

Method II: we were looking for the best image rotation angle, i.e. when the difference between latitudes of spots on the current and previous drawings is small (first run) and when the difference between latitudes of spots on the current and next drawings is small (second run). The result is a weighted mean of these two runs. The rotation of the image was not limited to any range of angles. Next, for each day we vary the time from the sunrise to the sunset and find sun ephemeris, i.e. P (the position angle of the northern extremity of the axis of rotation measured eastwards from the North Point of the solar disk), q - parallactic angle. These two parameters define the angle between solar axis and zenith direction. which is (P-q). Finally, we choose the time when (P-q) was equal to the rotation angle we found before.
There are 62 days when the rotation angle does not match to any time between sunrise and sunset.


Draw - number of drawing according to Harriot’s numeration;
Place - location of observation;
YYYY - Year;
MM - Month;
DD - Day;
HH - UT Hour (Time of observation defined by us);
MI- Minute (Time of observation defined by us);
G - Arbitrary number of a sunspot group;
Sp - Arbitrary number of a sunspot;
BBB.BB - Heliographic latitude. Southern latitudes are negative;
LLL.LL - Heliographic longitude in the Carrington rotation frame;
B0 - Heliographic latitude of apparent disk center;
L0 - Heliographic longitude of apparent disk center;
P - Position angle;
Rot - Rotation angle of solar image in x-y plane;
q - Parallactic angle;
Alt - Altitude;
Azm - Azimuth;
Area - Area in millionths of the solar hemisphere (msh);
alpha - angular distance on the surface of the Sun from the center of the disk to the object;
time_1  time_2 and time_3 - Time of observation noted by Harriot.
